201401	2344	2014-01-29	meeting	BERNANKE	Thank you.	23	2
201401	2345	2014-01-29	meeting	BERNANKE	President Kocherlakota.	23	2
201401	2346	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am going to deviate from the example set by President Lacker.	23	2
201401	2347	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	For today, Mr Chairman, I am willing to support alternative B.	23	2
201401	2348	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	As others have noted, with the unemployment rate nearing 6.5 percent, I believe it will be important in the near term to change our forward guidance for the fed funds rate.	23	2
201401	2349	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So I’ll spend my time talking about potential changes in the language that we could be thinking about for March or April.	23	2
201401	2350	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’ll be giving some context regarding what I see as the main lessons learned about communication in 2013.	23	2
201401	2351	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this context is important because my lessons learned will deviate from the lessons learned by others around the table, and I think that’s leading us to different conclusions.	23	2
201401	2352	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We had two kinds of communication in place at the beginning of 2013.	23	2
201401	2353	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We had qualitative communication in place about the end of the asset purchase program, with a key marker being described as substantial improvement in the labor market outlook.	23	2
201401	2354	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We also had quantitative communication in place about the evolution of the fed funds rate.	23	2
201401	2355	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, when I look back at 2013, I see that the latter, quantitative communication was more effective.	23	2
201401	2356	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The qualitative communication about the asset purchase program created two significant and related problems for us.	23	2
201401	2357	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	First, market expectations about the meaning of “substantial improvement in the labor market outlook” evolved in ways that we could not control, and the ultimate size of the program ended up being much larger than most or maybe even all of us anticipated, especially given the fall in the unemployment rate that has actually transpired.	23	2
201401	2358	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Second, and relatedly, the Committee ultimately had to disappoint financial markets.	23	2
201401	2359	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That process led to a very bumpy ride in financial markets in the middle of the year, and I think we were quite lucky that it did not end up having broader economic impacts.	23	2
201401	2360	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In contrast, the fed funds rate communication worked well over the course of 2013 to pin down market expectations.	23	2
201401	2361	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	There was a slight blip in fed funds rate expectations in June and July, but I think it’s reasonable to attribute that blip entirely to communications challenges associated with the asset purchase program.	23	2
201401	2362	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And we were able to work through that blip and bring market expectations in alignment with our own because we had the quantitative guidance in place to refer to.	23	2
201401	2363	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So over the course of the year, I would say markets remained convinced that we would not raise rates until the unemployment rate fell below 6.5 percent.	23	2
201401	2364	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	A number of people have expressed concerns about using the unemployment rate as a threshold marker and, I guess, regret having used it in the first place because the unemployment rate is providing an overly optimistic reading of labor market health.	23	2
201401	2365	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That is an opinion I have certainly expressed publicly—that it might well be true that the unemployment rate is sending too optimistic a signal.	23	2
201401	2366	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But I think it’s critical to distinguish between thresholds and triggers here.	23	2
201401	2367	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	This is a very strong argument against using any particular metric, and, in particular, U-3, the unemployment rate, as a trigger for raising the fed funds rate.	23	2
201401	2368	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It underscores the importance and the strength of the threshold approach, where we explicitly retained optionality against exactly this kind of contingency.	23	2
201401	2369	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We didn’t put a trigger in place saying that we were going to raise rates as soon as unemployment fell below 6.5 percent exactly because we were concerned about the possibility that, in fact, the labor markets might not be as strong as that measure indicated.	23	2
201401	2370	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So the lessons of 2013 have convinced me—anew, I would say—that effective monetary policy at the zero lower bound really requires a quantitative approach to forward guidance.	23	2
201401	2371	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And I agree with you, Mr Chairman—right now, the qualitative approach that we laid out in December is working effectively.	23	2
201401	2372	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But it’s something that is going to work effectively until it doesn’t work effectively, and then we are going to have to try to deal with market volatility and figure out ways to do so on the fly, as we ended up doing in 2013.	23	2
201401	2373	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think it’s better to have a quantitative approach in place that will pin down expectations to begin with.	23	2
201401	2374	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Right now, I think our current communication really ignores what I would consider the lessons learned from 2013.	23	2
201401	2375	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Does “well past the time” mean nine months, as in Tealbook A?	23	2
201401	2376	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Or does it mean until the unemployment rate has fallen below 6 percent, as in Tealbook B?	23	2
201401	2377	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m concerned that, just as we saw with the LSAP program last year, it is going to be increasingly difficult for us to manage public expectations about the meaning of this statement as the unemployment rate falls below 6.5 percent, as we all begin, in our own separate communications, to opine on what the meaning of that statement is.	23	2
201401	2378	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Okay.	23	2
201401	2379	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I have argued strongly for quantitative language.	23	2
201401	2380	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	What kind of quantitative language should we use?	23	2
201401	2381	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The threshold approach definitely has its drawbacks, and if you wanted me to argue on that side, I could point to drawbacks.	23	2
201401	2382	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But it is important in communication not to let the perfect be the enemy of the good.	23	2
201401	2383	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Market participants have, I think, grown to understand the threshold approach.	23	2
201401	2384	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And I think it offers us a good mix of commitment and optionality.	23	2
201401	2385	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	For these reasons, I think a good starting point for consideration is that, in March, we should be committing to keep the fed funds rate extraordinarily low at least until the unemployment rate falls below some threshold lower than 6.5 percent.	23	2
201401	2386	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m sympathetic to some of the comments that President Plosser made about maybe putting a little more weight on the inflation rate, and I’ll come back to that in a second.	23	2
201401	2387	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, what threshold, exactly, should we be picking?	23	2
201401	2388	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One thing I learned in 2013 is that we are very reluctant to move thresholds downward, which was a little bit of a surprise to me because I viewed that as always an option before us.	23	2
201401	2389	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But it is clear the Committee has that sense.	23	2
201401	2390	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So when we do adopt the threshold, it should really be low enough that we don’t see a substantial chance of later wishing it were even lower.	23	2
201401	2391	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In the economics go-round, I have argued there are good reasons to have lowered our estimates of the long-run mandate-consistent unemployment rate relative to a year ago.	23	2
201401	2392	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	For both of these reasons, I would prefer 5.5 percent.	23	2
201401	2393	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Why wouldn’t we adopt such a commitment?	23	2
201401	2394	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think this comes back to where our estimates of the long-run unemployment rate are.	23	2
201401	2395	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Some participants have estimates of the long- run unemployment rate as high as 6 percent.	23	2
201401	2396	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am suggesting keeping the fed funds rate extraordinarily low until the unemployment rate falls below 5.5 percent.	23	2
201401	2397	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Those participants might be concerned that such a policy stance could lead to undue pressures on inflation or risks to financial stability.	23	2
201401	2398	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So let me talk about how to deal with each of those possibilities in turn.	23	2
201401	2399	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	In terms of inflation, I actually think alternative A offers the right way to proceed on this.	23	2
201401	2400	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’d say we should be keeping the fed funds rate extremely low until the unemployment rate falls below 5.5 percent.	23	2
201401	2401	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We could lead by saying we are going to be keeping the federal funds rate extraordinarily low at least until one of the following conditions is satisfied, and the first condition could be that the medium-term outlook for inflation—the one- to two-year-ahead outlook—is 2 percent.	23	2
201401	2402	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I’m perfectly happy to have that as the lead condition, because it fits in with President Evans’s view that one way to explain and articulate policy is through our goals.	23	2
201401	2403	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And we are going to wait until we actually see the outlook for inflation return to 2 percent.	23	2
201401	2404	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	That, I think, puts in a guardrail.	23	2
201401	2405	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	If you are really worried about inflationary pressures, they should show up in that one- to two-year-ahead outlook for inflation.	23	2
201401	2406	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The second condition would be, as I said, that the unemployment rate falls below 5.5 percent.	23	2
201401	2407	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Now, the third issue is one that we did not deal with when we laid out our first threshold and that we should be dealing with now, which is that committing to this kind of strategy could lead to undue risks to financial stability.	23	2
201401	2408	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the right way to deal with this is to add a third knockout clause—a third condition that would lead us to consider raising rates.	23	2
201401	2409	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	It would essentially be a financial-stability knockout clause along the lines of the Bank of England’s— language that would allow the Committee the option of raising rates if the Committee saw that doing so would produce sufficient benefits in terms of mitigating potential risks to financial stability.	23	2
201401	2410	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So it would be very open-ended and would allow us, essentially on a meeting-by- meeting basis, to talk it through, assess what’s going on in the financial markets, and see if raising rates would be effective in that regard.	23	2
201401	2411	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	So that’s my three-pronged suggestion in terms of forward guidance.	23	2
201401	2412	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	We can commit to keeping rates extraordinarily low at least until the medium-term outlook—the one- to two-year- ahead outlook—for inflation has gone back to 2 percent, or the unemployment rate has fallen below 5.5 percent, or whatever the financial-stability knockout clause looks like.	23	2
201401	2413	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And I agree with what’s been said before—I think we have to move quickly.	23	2
201401	2414	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think March will be a very good time to do this.	23	2
201401	2415	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	One last point.	23	2
201401	2416	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I am sympathetic to President Bullard’s desire to have a press conference every meeting.	23	2
201401	2417	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	Especially given that I am not the one doing it, I think it seems very attractive.	23	2
201401	2418	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	But in all seriousness, I’m concerned about the governance.	23	2
201401	2419	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	I think the Committee really should take responsibility for what monetary policy is.	23	2
201401	2420	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	The right way to take that responsibility is through the statement.	23	2
201401	2421	2014-01-29	meeting	KOCHERLAKOTA	And I think we should be working to make the statement an effective communication of our collective views.	23	2
